    34	
    35	// Allocate 32 digits for the line number.
    36	// An estimate is that we can print about 1e8 lines/seconds, so 32 digits
    37	// would be enough for billions of universe lifetimes.
    38	const LINE_NUMBER_BUF_SIZE: usize = 32;
    39	
    40	struct LineNumber {
    41	    buf: [u8; LINE_NUMBER_BUF_SIZE],
    42	    print_start: usize,
    43	    num_start: usize,
    44	    num_end: usize,
    45	}
    46	
    47	// Logic to store a string for the line number. Manually incrementing the value
    48	// represented in a buffer like this is significantly faster than storing
    49	// a `usize` and using the standard Rust formatting macros to format a `usize`
    50	// to a string each time it's needed.
    51	// Buffer is initialized to "     1\t" and incremented each time `increment` is
    52	// called, using uucore's fast_inc function that operates on strings.
    53	impl LineNumber {
    54	    fn new() -> Self {
    55	        let mut buf = [b'0'; LINE_NUMBER_BUF_SIZE];
    56	
    57	        let init_str = "     1\t";
    58	        let print_start = buf.len() - init_str.len();
    59	        let num_start = buf.len() - 2;
    60	        let num_end = buf.len() - 1;
    61	
    62	        buf[print_start..].copy_from_slice(init_str.as_bytes());
    63	
    64	        LineNumber {
    65	            buf,
    66	            print_start,
    67	            num_start,
    68	            num_end,
    69	        }
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    fn increment(&mut self) {
    73	        fast_inc_one(&mut self.buf, &mut self.num_start, self.num_end);
    74	        self.print_start = self.print_start.min(self.num_start);
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    #[inline]
    78	    fn to_str(&self) -> &[u8] {
    79	        &self.buf[self.print_start..]
    80	    }
    81	
    82	    fn write(&self, writer: &mut impl Write) -> io::Result<()> {
    83	        writer.write_all(self.to_str())
    84	    }
    85	}
    86	
    87	#[derive(Error, Debug)]
    88	enum CatError {
    89	    /// Wrapper around `io::Error`
    90	    #[error("{0}")]
    91	    Io(#[from] io::Error),
    92	    /// Wrapper around `nix::Error`
    93	    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    94	    #[error("{0}")]
    95	    Nix(#[from] nix::Error),
    96	    /// Unknown file type; it's not a regular file, socket, etc.
    97	    #[error("unknown filetype: {ft_debug}")]
    98	    UnknownFiletype {
    99	        /// A debug print of the file type
   100	        ft_debug: String,
   101	    },
   102	    #[error("Is a directory")]
   103	    IsDirectory,
   104	    #[error("input file is output file")]
   105	    OutputIsInput,
   106	    #[error("Too many levels of symbolic links")]
   107	    TooManySymlinks,
   108	}
   109	
   110	type CatResult<T> = Result<T, CatError>;
   111	
   112	#[derive(PartialEq)]
   113	enum NumberingMode {
   114	    None,
   115	    NonEmpty,
   116	    All,
   117	}
   118	
   119	struct OutputOptions {
   120	    /// Line numbering mode
   121	    number: NumberingMode,
   122	
   123	    /// Suppress repeated empty output lines
   124	    squeeze_blank: bool,
   125	
   126	    /// display TAB characters as `tab`
   127	    show_tabs: bool,
   128	
   129	    /// Show end of lines
   130	    show_ends: bool,
   131	
   132	    /// use ^ and M- notation, except for LF (\\n) and TAB (\\t)
   133	    show_nonprint: bool,
   134	}
   135	
   136	impl OutputOptions {
   137	    fn tab(&self) -> &'static str {
   138	        if self.show_tabs { "^I" } else { "\t" }
   139	    }
   140	
   141	    fn end_of_line(&self) -> &'static str {
   142	        if self.show_ends { "$\n" } else { "\n" }
   143	    }
   144	
   145	    /// We can write fast if we can simply copy the contents of the file to
   146	    /// stdout, without augmenting the output with e.g. line numbers.
   147	    fn can_write_fast(&self) -> bool {
   148	        !(self.show_tabs
   149	            || self.show_nonprint
   150	            || self.show_ends
   151	            || self.squeeze_blank
   152	            || self.number != NumberingMode::None)
   153	    }
   154	}
   155	
   156	/// State that persists between output of each file. This struct is only used
   157	/// when we can't write fast.
   158	struct OutputState {
   159	    /// The current line number
   160	    line_number: LineNumber,
   161	
   162	    /// Whether the output cursor is at the beginning of a new line
   163	    at_line_start: bool,
   164	
   165	    /// Whether we skipped a \r, which still needs to be printed
   166	    skipped_carriage_return: bool,
   167	
   168	    /// Whether we have already printed a blank line
   169	    one_blank_kept: bool,
   170	}
   171	
   172	#[cfg(unix)]
   173	trait FdReadable: Read + AsFd {}
   174	#[cfg(not(unix))]
   175	trait FdReadable: Read {}
   176	
   177	#[cfg(unix)]
   178	impl<T> FdReadable for T where T: Read + AsFd {}
   179	#[cfg(not(unix))]
   180	impl<T> FdReadable for T where T: Read {}
   181	
   182	/// Represents an open file handle, stream, or other device
   183	struct InputHandle<R: FdReadable> {
   184	    reader: R,
   185	    is_interactive: bool,
   186	}
   187	
   188	/// Concrete enum of recognized file types.
   189	///
   190	/// *Note*: `cat`-ing a directory should result in an
   191	/// [`CatError::IsDirectory`]
   192	enum InputType {
   193	    Directory,
   194	    File,
   195	    StdIn,
   196	    SymLink,
   197	    #[cfg(unix)]
   198	    BlockDevice,
   199	    #[cfg(unix)]
   200	    CharacterDevice,
   201	    #[cfg(unix)]
   202	    Fifo,
   203	    #[cfg(unix)]
   204	    Socket,
   205	}

   207	mod options {
   208	    pub static FILE: &str = "file";
   209	    pub static SHOW_ALL: &str = "show-all";
   210	    pub static NUMBER_NONBLANK: &str = "number-nonblank";
   211	    pub static SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS: &str = "e";
   212	    pub static SHOW_ENDS: &str = "show-ends";
   213	    pub static NUMBER: &str = "number";
   214	    pub static SQUEEZE_BLANK: &str = "squeeze-blank";
   215	    pub static SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS: &str = "t";
   216	    pub static SHOW_TABS: &str = "show-tabs";
   217	    pub static SHOW_NONPRINTING: &str = "show-nonprinting";
   218	    pub static IGNORED_U: &str = "ignored-u";
   219	}
   220	
   221	#[uucore::main]
   222	pub fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
   223	    let matches = uu_app().try_get_matches_from(args)?;
   224	
   225	    let number_mode = if matches.get_flag(options::NUMBER_NONBLANK) {
   226	        NumberingMode::NonEmpty
   227	    } else if matches.get_flag(options::NUMBER) {
   228	        NumberingMode::All
   229	    } else {
   230	        NumberingMode::None
   231	    };
   232	
   233	    let show_nonprint = [
   234	        options::SHOW_ALL.to_owned(),
   235	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS.to_owned(),
   236	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS.to_owned(),
   237	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING.to_owned(),
   238	    ]
   239	    .iter()
   240	    .any(|v| matches.get_flag(v));
   241	
   242	    let show_ends = [
   243	        options::SHOW_ENDS.to_owned(),
   244	        options::SHOW_ALL.to_owned(),
   245	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS.to_owned(),
   246	    ]
   247	    .iter()
   248	    .any(|v| matches.get_flag(v));
   249	
   250	    let show_tabs = [
   251	        options::SHOW_ALL.to_owned(),
   252	        options::SHOW_TABS.to_owned(),
   253	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS.to_owned(),
   254	    ]
   255	    .iter()
   256	    .any(|v| matches.get_flag(v));
   257	
   258	    let squeeze_blank = matches.get_flag(options::SQUEEZE_BLANK);
   259	    let files: Vec<String> = match matches.get_many::<String>(options::FILE) {
   260	        Some(v) => v.cloned().collect(),
   261	        None => vec!["-".to_owned()],
   262	    };
   263	
   264	    let options = OutputOptions {
   265	        show_ends,
   266	        number: number_mode,
   267	        show_nonprint,
   268	        show_tabs,
   269	        squeeze_blank,
   270	    };
   271	    cat_files(&files, &options)
   272	}
   273	
   274	pub fn uu_app() -> Command {
   275	    Command::new(uucore::util_name())
   276	        .version(uucore::crate_version!())
   277	        .override_usage(format_usage(&get_message("cat-usage")))
   278	        .about(get_message("cat-about"))
   279	        .infer_long_args(true)
   280	        .args_override_self(true)
   281	        .arg(
   282	            Arg::new(options::FILE)
   283	                .hide(true)
   284	                .action(ArgAction::Append)
   285	                .value_hint(clap::ValueHint::FilePath),
   286	        )
   287	        .arg(
   288	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_ALL)
   289	                .short('A')
   290	                .long(options::SHOW_ALL)
   291	                .help("equivalent to -vET")
   292	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   293	        )
   294	        .arg(
   295	            Arg::new(options::NUMBER_NONBLANK)
   296	                .short('b')
   297	                .long(options::NUMBER_NONBLANK)
   298	                .help("number nonempty output lines, overrides -n")
   299	                // Note: This MUST NOT .overrides_with(options::NUMBER)!
   300	                // In clap, overriding is symmetric, so "-b -n" counts as "-n", which is not what we want.
   301	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   302	        )
   303	        .arg(
   304	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS)
   305	                .short('e')
   306	                .help("equivalent to -vE")
   307	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   308	        )
   309	        .arg(
   310	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_ENDS)
   311	                .short('E')
   312	                .long(options::SHOW_ENDS)
   313	                .help("display $ at end of each line")
   314	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   315	        )
   316	        .arg(
   317	            Arg::new(options::NUMBER)
   318	                .short('n')
   319	                .long(options::NUMBER)
   320	                .help("number all output lines")
   321	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   322	        )
   323	        .arg(
   324	            Arg::new(options::SQUEEZE_BLANK)
   325	                .short('s')
   326	                .long(options::SQUEEZE_BLANK)
   327	                .help("suppress repeated empty output lines")
   328	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   329	        )
   330	        .arg(
   331	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS)
   332	                .short('t')
   333	                .help("equivalent to -vT")
   334	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   335	        )
   336	        .arg(
   337	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_TABS)
   338	                .short('T')
   339	                .long(options::SHOW_TABS)
   340	                .help("display TAB characters at ^I")
   341	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   342	        )
   343	        .arg(
   344	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING)
   345	                .short('v')
   346	                .long(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING)
   347	                .help("use ^ and M- notation, except for LF (\\n) and TAB (\\t)")
   348	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   349	        )
   350	        .arg(
   351	            Arg::new(options::IGNORED_U)
   352	                .short('u')
   353	                .help("(ignored)")
   354	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   355	        )
   356	}
   357	
   358	fn cat_handle<R: FdReadable>(
   359	    handle: &mut InputHandle<R>,
   360	    options: &OutputOptions,
   361	    state: &mut OutputState,
   362	) -> CatResult<()> {
   363	    if options.can_write_fast() {
   364	        write_fast(handle)
   365	    } else {
   366	        write_lines(handle, options, state)
   367	    }
   368	}
   369	
   370	fn cat_path(path: &str, options: &OutputOptions, state: &mut OutputState) -> CatResult<()> {
   371	    match get_input_type(path)? {
   372	        InputType::StdIn => {
   373	            let stdin = io::stdin();
   374	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&stdin, &io::stdout()) {
   375	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   376	            }
   377	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   378	                reader: stdin,
   379	                is_interactive: io::stdin().is_terminal(),
   380	            };
   381	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   382	        }
   383	        InputType::Directory => Err(CatError::IsDirectory),
   384	        #[cfg(unix)]
   385	        InputType::Socket => {
   386	            let socket = UnixStream::connect(path)?;
   387	            socket.shutdown(Shutdown::Write)?;
   388	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   389	                reader: socket,
   390	                is_interactive: false,
   391	            };
   392	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   393	        }
   394	        _ => {
   395	            let file = File::open(path)?;
   396	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&file, &io::stdout()) {
   397	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   398	            }
   399	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   400	                reader: file,
   401	                is_interactive: false,
   402	            };
   403	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   404	        }
   405	    }
   406	}
   407	
   408	fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
   409	    let mut state = OutputState {
   410	        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
   411	        at_line_start: true,
   412	        skipped_carriage_return: false,
   413	        one_blank_kept: false,
   414	    };
   415	    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();
   416	
   417	    for path in files {
   418	        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
   419	            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
   420	        }
   421	    }
   422	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   423	        print!("\r");
   424	    }
   425	    if error_messages.is_empty() {
   426	        Ok(())
   427	    } else {
   428	        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
   429	        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());
   430	
   431	        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(
   432	            error_messages.len() as i32,
   433	            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),
   434	        ))
   435	    }
   436	}
   437	
   438	/// Classifies the `InputType` of file at `path` if possible
   439	///
   440	/// # Arguments
   441	///
   442	/// * `path` - Path on a file system to classify metadata
   443	fn get_input_type(path: &str) -> CatResult<InputType> {
   444	    if path == "-" {
   445	        return Ok(InputType::StdIn);
   446	    }
   447	
   448	    let ft = match metadata(path) {
   449	        Ok(md) => md.file_type(),
   450	        Err(e) => {
   451	            if let Some(raw_error) = e.raw_os_error() {
   452	                // On Unix-like systems, the error code for "Too many levels of symbolic links" is 40 (ELOOP).
   453	                // we want to provide a proper error message in this case.
   454	                #[cfg(not(any(target_os = "macos", target_os = "freebsd")))]
   455	                let too_many_symlink_code = 40;
   456	                #[cfg(any(target_os = "macos", target_os = "freebsd"))]
   457	                let too_many_symlink_code = 62;
   458	                if raw_error == too_many_symlink_code {
   459	                    return Err(CatError::TooManySymlinks);
   460	                }
   461	            }
   462	            return Err(CatError::Io(e));
   463	        }
   464	    };
   465	    match ft {
   466	        #[cfg(unix)]
   467	        ft if ft.is_block_device() => Ok(InputType::BlockDevice),
   468	        #[cfg(unix)]
   469	        ft if ft.is_char_device() => Ok(InputType::CharacterDevice),
   470	        #[cfg(unix)]
   471	        ft if ft.is_fifo() => Ok(InputType::Fifo),
   472	        #[cfg(unix)]
   473	        ft if ft.is_socket() => Ok(InputType::Socket),
   474	        ft if ft.is_dir() => Ok(InputType::Directory),
   475	        ft if ft.is_file() => Ok(InputType::File),
   476	        ft if ft.is_symlink() => Ok(InputType::SymLink),
   477	        _ => Err(CatError::UnknownFiletype {
   478	            ft_debug: format!("{ft:?}"),
   479	        }),
   480	    }
   481	}
   482	
   483	/// Writes handle to stdout with no configuration. This allows a
   484	/// simple memory copy.
   485	fn write_fast<R: FdReadable>(handle: &mut InputHandle<R>) -> CatResult<()> {
   486	    let stdout = io::stdout();
   487	    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
   488	    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   489	    {
   490	        // If we're on Linux or Android, try to use the splice() system call
   491	        // for faster writing. If it works, we're done.
   492	        if !splice::write_fast_using_splice(handle, &stdout_lock)? {
   493	            return Ok(());
   494	        }
   495	    }
   496	    // If we're not on Linux or Android, or the splice() call failed,
   497	    // fall back on slower writing.
   498	    let mut buf = [0; 1024 * 64];
   499	    loop {
   500	        match handle.reader.read(&mut buf) {
   501	            Ok(n) => {
   502	                if n == 0 {
   503	                    break;
   504	                }
   505	                stdout_lock.write_all(&buf[..n])?;
   506	            }
   507	            Err(e) => return Err(e.into()),
   508	        }
   509	    }
   510	
   511	    // If the splice() call failed and there has been some data written to
   512	    // stdout via while loop above AND there will be second splice() call
   513	    // that will succeed, data pushed through splice will be output before
   514	    // the data buffered in stdout.lock. Therefore additional explicit flush
   515	    // is required here.
   516	    stdout_lock.flush()?;
   517	    Ok(())
   518	}
   519

   521	/// propagating any errors that might occur.
   522	fn write_lines<R: FdReadable>(

   520	/// Outputs file contents to stdout in a line-by-line fashion,
   521	/// propagating any errors that might occur.
   522	fn write_lines<R: FdReadable>(
   523	    handle: &mut InputHandle<R>,
   524	    options: &OutputOptions,
   525	    state: &mut OutputState,
   526	) -> CatResult<()> {
   527	    let mut in_buf = [0; 1024 * 31];
   528	    let stdout = io::stdout();
   529	    let stdout = stdout.lock();
   530	    // Add a 32K buffer for stdout - this greatly improves performance.
   531	    let mut writer = BufWriter::with_capacity(32 * 1024, stdout);
   532	
   533	    while let Ok(n) = handle.reader.read(&mut in_buf) {
   534	        if n == 0 {
   535	            break;
   536	        }
   537	        let in_buf = &in_buf[..n];
   538	        let mut pos = 0;
   539	        while pos < n {
   540	            // skip empty line_number enumerating them if needed
   541	            if in_buf[pos] == b'\n' {
   542	                write_new_line(&mut writer, options, state, handle.is_interactive)?;
   543	                state.at_line_start = true;
   544	                pos += 1;
   545	                continue;
   546	            }
   547	            if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   548	                writer.write_all(b"\r")?;
   549	                state.skipped_carriage_return = false;
   550	                state.at_line_start = false;
   551	            }
   552	            state.one_blank_kept = false;
   553	            if state.at_line_start && options.number != NumberingMode::None {
   554	                state.line_number.write(&mut writer)?;
   555	                state.line_number.increment();
   556	            }
   557	
   558	            // print to end of line or end of buffer
   559	            let offset = write_end(&mut writer, &in_buf[pos..], options);
   560	
   561	            // end of buffer?
   562	            if offset + pos == in_buf.len() {
   563	                state.at_line_start = false;
   564	                break;
   565	            }
   566	            if in_buf[pos + offset] == b'\r' {
   567	                state.skipped_carriage_return = true;
   568	            } else {
   569	                assert_eq!(in_buf[pos + offset], b'\n');
   570	                // print suitable end of line
   571	                write_end_of_line(
   572	                    &mut writer,
   573	                    options.end_of_line().as_bytes(),
   574	                    handle.is_interactive,
   575	                )?;
   576	                state.at_line_start = true;
   577	            }
   578	            pos += offset + 1;
   579	        }
   580	        // We need to flush the buffer each time around the loop in order to pass GNU tests.
   581	        // When we are reading the input from a pipe, the `handle.reader.read` call at the top
   582	        // of this loop will block (indefinitely) whist waiting for more data. The expectation
   583	        // however is that anything that's ready for output should show up in the meantime,
   584	        // and not be buffered internally to the `cat` process.
   585	        // Hence it's necessary to flush our buffer before every time we could potentially block
   586	        // on a `std::io::Read::read` call.
   587	        writer.flush()?;
   588	    }
   589	
   590	    Ok(())
   591	}

   596	    options: &OutputOptions,
   597	    state: &mut OutputState,
   598	    is_interactive: bool,
   599	) -> CatResult<()> {
   600	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {

     1	// This file is part of the uutils coreutils package.
     2	//
     3	// For the full copyright and license information, please view the LICENSE
     4	// file that was distributed with this source code.
     5	//! All utils return exit with an exit code. Usually, the following scheme is used:
     6	//! * `0`: succeeded
     7	//! * `1`: minor problems
     8	//! * `2`: major problems
     9	//!
    10	//! This module provides types to reconcile these exit codes with idiomatic Rust error
    11	//! handling. This has a couple advantages over manually using [`std::process::exit`]:
    12	//! 1. It enables the use of `?`, `map_err`, `unwrap_or`, etc. in `uumain`.
    13	//! 1. It encourages the use of [`UResult`]/[`Result`] in functions in the utils.
    14	//! 1. The error messages are largely standardized across utils.
    15	//! 1. Standardized error messages can be created from external result types
    16	//!    (i.e. [`std::io::Result`] & `clap::ClapResult`).
    17	//! 1. [`set_exit_code`] takes away the burden of manually tracking exit codes for non-fatal errors.
    18	//!
    19	//! # Usage
    20	//! The signature of a typical util should be:
    21	//! ```ignore
    22	//! fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
    23	//!     ...
    24	//! }
    25	//! ```
    26	//! [`UResult`] is a simple wrapper around [`Result`] with a custom error trait: [`UError`]. The
    27	//! most important difference with types implementing [`std::error::Error`] is that [`UError`]s
    28	//! can specify the exit code of the program when they are returned from `uumain`:
    29	//! * When `Ok` is returned, the code set with [`set_exit_code`] is used as exit code. If
    30	//!   [`set_exit_code`] was not used, then `0` is used.
    31	//! * When `Err` is returned, the code corresponding with the error is used as exit code and the
    32	//!   error message is displayed.
    33	//!
    34	//! Additionally, the errors can be displayed manually with the [`crate::show`] and [`crate::show_if_err`] macros:
    35	//! ```ignore
    36	//! let res = Err(USimpleError::new(1, "Error!!"));
    37	//! show_if_err!(res);
    38	//! // or
    39	//! if let Err(e) = res {
    40	//!    show!(e);
    41	//! }
    42	//! ```
    43	//!
    44	//! **Note**: The [`crate::show`] and [`crate::show_if_err`] macros set the exit code of the program using
    45	//! [`set_exit_code`]. See the documentation on that function for more information.
    46	//!
    47	//! # Guidelines
    48	//! * Use error types from `uucore` where possible.
    49	//! * Add error types to `uucore` if an error appears in multiple utils.
    50	//! * Prefer proper custom error types over [`ExitCode`] and [`USimpleError`].
    51	//! * [`USimpleError`] may be used in small utils with simple error handling.
    52	//! * Using [`ExitCode`] is not recommended but can be useful for converting utils to use
    53	//!   [`UResult`].
    54	
    55	// spell-checker:ignore uioerror rustdoc
    56	
    57	use std::{
    58	    error::Error,
    59	    fmt::{Display, Formatter},
    60	    sync::atomic::{AtomicI32, Ordering},
    61	};
    62	
    63	static EXIT_CODE: AtomicI32 = AtomicI32::new(0);
    64	
    65	/// Get the last exit code set with [`set_exit_code`].
    66	/// The default value is `0`.
    67	pub fn get_exit_code() -> i32 {
    68	    EXIT_CODE.load(Ordering::SeqCst)
    69	}
    70	
    71	/// Set the exit code for the program if `uumain` returns `Ok(())`.
    72	///
    73	/// This function is most useful for non-fatal errors, for example when applying an operation to
    74	/// multiple files:
    75	/// ```ignore
    76	/// use uucore::error::{UResult, set_exit_code};
    77	///
    78	/// fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
    79	///     ...
    80	///     for file in files {
    81	///         let res = some_operation_that_might_fail(file);
    82	///         match res {
    83	///             Ok() => {},
    84	///             Err(_) => set_exit_code(1),
    85	///         }
    86	///     }
    87	///     Ok(()) // If any of the operations failed, 1 is returned.
    88	/// }
    89	/// ```
    90	pub fn set_exit_code(code: i32) {
    91	    EXIT_CODE.store(code, Ordering::SeqCst);
    92	}
    93	
    94	/// Result type that should be returned by all utils.
    95	pub type UResult<T> = Result<T, Box<dyn UError>>;
    96	
    97	/// Custom errors defined by the utils and `uucore`.
    98	///
    99	/// All errors should implement [`std::error::Error`], [`std::fmt::Display`] and
   100	/// [`std::fmt::Debug`] and have an additional `code` method that specifies the
   101	/// exit code of the program if the error is returned from `uumain`.
   102	///
   103	/// An example of a custom error from `ls`:
   104	///
   105	/// ```
   106	/// use uucore::{
   107	///     display::Quotable,
   108	///     error::{UError, UResult}
   109	/// };
   110	/// use std::{
   111	///     error::Error,
   112	///     fmt::{Display, Debug},
   113	///     path::PathBuf
   114	/// };
   115	///
   116	/// #[derive(Debug)]
   117	/// enum LsError {
   118	///     InvalidLineWidth(String),
   119	///     NoMetadata(PathBuf),
   120	/// }
   121	///
   122	/// impl UError for LsError {
   123	///     fn code(&self) -> i32 {
   124	///         match self {
   125	///             LsError::InvalidLineWidth(_) => 2,
   126	///             LsError::NoMetadata(_) => 1,
   127	///         }
   128	///     }
   129	/// }
   130	///
   131	/// impl Error for LsError {}
   132	///
   133	/// impl Display for LsError {
   134	///     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   135	///         match self {
   136	///             LsError::InvalidLineWidth(s) => write!(f, "invalid line width: {}", s.quote()),
   137	///             LsError::NoMetadata(p) => write!(f, "could not open file: {}", p.quote()),
   138	///         }
   139	///     }
   140	/// }
   141	/// ```
   142	///
   143	/// The main routine would look like this:
   144	///
   145	/// ```ignore
   146	/// #[uucore::main]
   147	/// pub fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
   148	///     // Perform computations here ...
   149	///     return Err(LsError::InvalidLineWidth(String::from("test")).into())
   150	/// }
   151	/// ```
   152	///
   153	/// The call to `into()` is required to convert the `LsError` to
   154	/// [`Box<dyn UError>`]. The implementation for `From` is provided automatically.
   155	///
   156	/// A crate like [`quick_error`](https://crates.io/crates/quick-error) might
   157	/// also be used, but will still require an `impl` for the `code` method.
   158	pub trait UError: Error + Send {
   159	    /// Error code of a custom error.
   160	    ///
   161	    /// Set a return value for each variant of an enum-type to associate an
   162	    /// error code (which is returned to the system shell) with an error
   163	    /// variant.
   164	    ///
   165	    /// # Example
   166	    ///
   167	    /// ```
   168	    /// use uucore::{
   169	    ///     display::Quotable,
   170	    ///     error::UError
   171	    /// };
   172	    /// use std::{
   173	    ///     error::Error,
   174	    ///     fmt::{Display, Debug},
   175	    ///     path::PathBuf
   176	    /// };
   177	    ///
   178	    /// #[derive(Debug)]
   179	    /// enum MyError {
   180	    ///     Foo(String),
   181	    ///     Bar(PathBuf),
   182	    ///     Bing(),
   183	    /// }
   184	    ///
   185	    /// impl UError for MyError {
   186	    ///     fn code(&self) -> i32 {
   187	    ///         match self {
   188	    ///             MyError::Foo(_) => 2,
   189	    ///             // All other errors yield the same error code, there's no
   190	    ///             // need to list them explicitly.
   191	    ///             _ => 1,
   192	    ///         }
   193	    ///     }
   194	    /// }
   195	    ///
   196	    /// impl Error for MyError {}
   197	    ///
   198	    /// impl Display for MyError {
   199	    ///     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   200	    ///         use MyError as ME;
   201	    ///         match self {
   202	    ///             ME::Foo(s) => write!(f, "Unknown Foo: {}", s.quote()),
   203	    ///             ME::Bar(p) => write!(f, "Couldn't find Bar: {}", p.quote()),
   204	    ///             ME::Bing() => write!(f, "Exterminate!"),
   205	    ///         }
   206	    ///     }
   207	    /// }
   208	    /// ```
   209	    fn code(&self) -> i32 {
   210	        1
   211	    }
   212	
   213	    /// Print usage help to a custom error.
   214	    ///
   215	    /// Return true or false to control whether a short usage help is printed
   216	    /// below the error message. The usage help is in the format: "Try `{name}
   217	    /// --help` for more information." and printed only if `true` is returned.
   218	    ///
   219	    /// # Example
   220	    ///
   221	    /// ```
   222	    /// use uucore::{
   223	    ///     display::Quotable,
   224	    ///     error::UError
   225	    /// };
   226	    /// use std::{
   227	    ///     error::Error,
   228	    ///     fmt::{Display, Debug},
   229	    ///     path::PathBuf
   230	    /// };
   231	    ///
   232	    /// #[derive(Debug)]
   233	    /// enum MyError {
   234	    ///     Foo(String),
   235	    ///     Bar(PathBuf),
   236	    ///     Bing(),
   237	    /// }
   238	    ///
   239	    /// impl UError for MyError {
   240	    ///     fn usage(&self) -> bool {
   241	    ///         match self {
   242	    ///             // This will have a short usage help appended
   243	    ///             MyError::Bar(_) => true,
   244	    ///             // These matches won't have a short usage help appended
   245	    ///             _ => false,
   246	    ///         }
   247	    ///     }
   248	    /// }
   249	    ///
   250	    /// impl Error for MyError {}
   251	    ///
   252	    /// impl Display for MyError {
   253	    ///     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   254	    ///         use MyError as ME;
   255	    ///         match self {
   256	    ///             ME::Foo(s) => write!(f, "Unknown Foo: {}", s.quote()),
   257	    ///             ME::Bar(p) => write!(f, "Couldn't find Bar: {}", p.quote()),
   258	    ///             ME::Bing() => write!(f, "Exterminate!"),
   259	    ///         }
   260	    ///     }
   261	    /// }
   262	    /// ```
   263	    fn usage(&self) -> bool {
   264	        false
   265	    }
   266	}
   267	
   268	impl<T> From<T> for Box<dyn UError>
   269	where
   270	    T: UError + 'static,
   271	{
   272	    fn from(t: T) -> Self {
   273	        Box::new(t)
   274	    }
   275	}
   276	
   277	/// A simple error type with an exit code and a message that implements [`UError`].
   278	///
   279	/// ```
   280	/// use uucore::error::{UResult, USimpleError};
   281	/// let err = USimpleError { code: 1, message: "error!".into()};
   282	/// let res: UResult<()> = Err(err.into());
   283	/// // or using the `new` method:
   284	/// let res: UResult<()> = Err(USimpleError::new(1, "error!"));
   285	/// ```
   286	#[derive(Debug)]
   287	pub struct USimpleError {
   288	    /// Exit code of the error.
   289	    pub code: i32,
   290	
   291	    /// Error message.
   292	    pub message: String,
   293	}
   294	
   295	impl USimpleError {
   296	    /// Create a new `USimpleError` with a given exit code and message.
   297	    #[allow(clippy::new_ret_no_self)]
   298	    pub fn new<S: Into<String>>(code: i32, message: S) -> Box<dyn UError> {
   299	        Box::new(Self {
   300	            code,
   301	            message: message.into(),
   302	        })
   303	    }
   304	}
   305	
   306	impl Error for USimpleError {}
   307	
   308	impl Display for USimpleError {
   309	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_>) -> Result<(), std::fmt::Error> {
   310	        self.message.fmt(f)
   311	    }
   312	}
   313	
   314	impl UError for USimpleError {
   315	    fn code(&self) -> i32 {
   316	        self.code
   317	    }
   318	}

   359	/// Wrapper type around [`std::io::Error`].
   360	///
   361	/// The messages displayed by [`UIoError`] should match the error messages displayed by GNU
   362	/// coreutils.
   363	///
   364	/// There are two ways to construct this type: with [`UIoError::new`] or by calling the
   365	/// [`FromIo::map_err_context`] method on a [`std::io::Result`] or [`std::io::Error`].
   366	/// ```
   367	/// use uucore::{
   368	///     display::Quotable,
   369	///     error::{FromIo, UResult, UIoError, UError}
   370	/// };
   371	/// use std::fs::File;
   372	/// use std::path::Path;
   373	/// let path = Path::new("test.txt");
   374	///
   375	/// // Manual construction
   376	/// let e: Box<dyn UError> = UIoError::new(
   377	///     std::io::ErrorKind::NotFound,
   378	///     format!("cannot access {}", path.quote())
   379	/// );
   380	/// let res: UResult<()> = Err(e.into());
   381	///
   382	/// // Converting from an `std::io::Error`.
   383	/// let res: UResult<File> = File::open(path).map_err_context(|| format!("cannot access {}", path.quote()));
   384	/// ```
   385	#[derive(Debug)]
   386	pub struct UIoError {
   387	    context: Option<String>,
   388	    inner: std::io::Error,
   389	}
   390	
   391	impl UIoError {
   392	    #[allow(clippy::new_ret_no_self)]
   393	    /// Create a new `UIoError` with a given exit code and message.
   394	    pub fn new<S: Into<String>>(kind: std::io::ErrorKind, context: S) -> Box<dyn UError> {
   395	        Box::new(Self {
   396	            context: Some(context.into()),
   397	            inner: kind.into(),
   398	        })
   399	    }
   400	}
   401	
   402	impl UError for UIoError {}
   403	
   404	impl Error for UIoError {}
   405	
   406	impl Display for UIoError {
   407	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_>) -> Result<(), std::fmt::Error> {
   408	        use std::io::ErrorKind::*;
   409	
   410	        let message;
   411	        let message = if self.inner.raw_os_error().is_some() {
   412	            // These are errors that come directly from the OS.
   413	            // We want to normalize their messages across systems,
   414	            // and we want to strip the "(os error X)" suffix.
   415	            match self.inner.kind() {
   416	                NotFound => "No such file or directory",
   417	                PermissionDenied => "Permission denied",
   418	                ConnectionRefused => "Connection refused",
   419	                ConnectionReset => "Connection reset",
   420	                ConnectionAborted => "Connection aborted",
   421	                NotConnected => "Not connected",
   422	                AddrInUse => "Address in use",
   423	                AddrNotAvailable => "Address not available",
   424	                BrokenPipe => "Broken pipe",
   425	                AlreadyExists => "Already exists",
   426	                WouldBlock => "Would block",
   427	                InvalidInput => "Invalid input",
   428	                InvalidData => "Invalid data",
   429	                TimedOut => "Timed out",
   430	                WriteZero => "Write zero",
   431	                Interrupted => "Interrupted",
   432	                UnexpectedEof => "Unexpected end of file",
   433	                _ => {
   434	                    // TODO: When the new error variants
   435	                    // (https://github.com/rust-lang/rust/issues/86442)
   436	                    // are stabilized, we should add them to the match statement.
   437	                    message = strip_errno(&self.inner);
   438	                    &message
   439	                }
   440	            }
   441	        } else {
   442	            // These messages don't need as much normalization, and the above
   443	            // messages wouldn't always be a good substitute.
   444	            // For example, ErrorKind::NotFound doesn't necessarily mean it was
   445	            // a file that was not found.
   446	            // There are also errors with entirely custom messages.
   447	            message = self.inner.to_string();
   448	            &message
   449	        };
   450	        if let Some(ctx) = &self.context {
   451	            write!(f, "{ctx}: {message}")
   452	        } else {
   453	            write!(f, "{message}")
   454	        }
   455	    }
   456	}
   457	
   458	/// Strip the trailing " (os error XX)" from io error strings.
   459	pub fn strip_errno(err: &std::io::Error) -> String {
   460	    let mut msg = err.to_string();
   461	    if let Some(pos) = msg.find(" (os error ") {
   462	        msg.truncate(pos);
   463	    }
   464	    msg
   465	}
   466	
   467	/// Enables the conversion from [`std::io::Error`] to [`UError`] and from [`std::io::Result`] to
   468	/// [`UResult`].
   469	pub trait FromIo<T> {
   470	    /// Map the error context of an [`std::io::Error`] or [`std::io::Result`] to a custom error
   471	    fn map_err_context(self, context: impl FnOnce() -> String) -> T;
   472	}
   473	
   474	impl FromIo<Box<UIoError>> for std::io::Error {
   475	    fn map_err_context(self, context: impl FnOnce() -> String) -> Box<UIoError> {
   476	        Box::new(UIoError {
   477	            context: Some(context()),
   478	            inner: self,
   479	        })
   480	    }
   481	}
   482	
   483	impl<T> FromIo<UResult<T>> for std::io::Result<T> {
   484	    fn map_err_context(self, context: impl FnOnce() -> String) -> UResult<T> {
   485	        self.map_err(|e| e.map_err_context(context) as Box<dyn UError>)
   486	    }
   487	}
   488	
   489	impl FromIo<Box<UIoError>> for std::io::ErrorKind {
   490	    fn map_err_context(self, context: impl FnOnce() -> String) -> Box<UIoError> {
   491	        Box::new(UIoError {
   492	            context: Some(context()),
   493	            inner: std::io::Error::new(self, ""),
   494	        })
   495	    }
   496	}
   497	
   498	impl From<std::io::Error> for UIoError {
   499	    fn from(f: std::io::Error) -> Self {
   500	        Self {
   501	            context: None,
   502	            inner: f,
   503	        }
   504	    }
   505	}
   506	
   507	impl From<std::io::Error> for Box<dyn UError> {
   508	    fn from(f: std::io::Error) -> Self {
   509	        let u_error: UIoError = f.into();
   510	        Box::new(u_error) as Self
   511	    }
   512	}

   408	fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
   409	    let mut state = OutputState {
   410	        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
   411	        at_line_start: true,
   412	        skipped_carriage_return: false,
   413	        one_blank_kept: false,
   414	    };
   415	    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();
   416	
   417	    for path in files {
   418	        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
   419	            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
   420	        }
   421	    }
   422	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   423	        print!("\r");
   424	    }
   425	    if error_messages.is_empty() {
   426	        Ok(())
   427	    } else {
   428	        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
   429	        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());
   430	
   431	        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(
   432	            error_messages.len() as i32,
   433	            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),
   434	        ))
   435	    }
   436	}

   370	fn cat_path(path: &str, options: &OutputOptions, state: &mut OutputState) -> CatResult<()> {
   371	    match get_input_type(path)? {
   372	        InputType::StdIn => {
   373	            let stdin = io::stdin();
   374	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&stdin, &io::stdout()) {
   375	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   376	            }
   377	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   378	                reader: stdin,
   379	                is_interactive: io::stdin().is_terminal(),
   380	            };
   381	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   382	        }
   383	        InputType::Directory => Err(CatError::IsDirectory),
   384	        #[cfg(unix)]
   385	        InputType::Socket => {
   386	            let socket = UnixStream::connect(path)?;
   387	            socket.shutdown(Shutdown::Write)?;
   388	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   389	                reader: socket,
   390	                is_interactive: false,
   391	            };
   392	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   393	        }
   394	        _ => {
   395	            let file = File::open(path)?;
   396	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&file, &io::stdout()) {
   397	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   398	            }
   399	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   400	                reader: file,
   401	                is_interactive: false,
   402	            };
   403	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   404	        }
   405	    }
   406	}

Now I need to apply this fix to the cat utility. The issue is that `cat` uses the `?` operator to propagate errors, so I need to either:
1. Check for BrokenPipe at the point where errors are caught (in `cat_files`)
2. Or handle it in the write functions themselves

Looking at the code, I think the best approach is to handle it in `cat_files` where errors are caught. Let me modify the code:

   408	fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
   409	    let mut state = OutputState {
   410	        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
   411	        at_line_start: true,
   412	        skipped_carriage_return: false,
   413	        one_blank_kept: false,
   414	    };
   415	    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();
   416	
   417	    for path in files {
   418	        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
   419	            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
   420	        }
   421	    }
   422	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   423	        print!("\r");
   424	    }
   425	    if error_messages.is_empty() {
   426	        Ok(())
   427	    } else {
   428	        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
   429	        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());
   430	
   431	        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(
   432	            error_messages.len() as i32,
   433	            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),
   434	        ))
   435	    }
   436	}

#[derive(PartialEq)]' --new_str 'type CatResult<T> = Result<T, CatError>;

impl CatError {
    /// Check if this error is a BrokenPipe error, which should be ignored
    fn is_broken_pipe(&self) -> bool {
        match self {
            CatError::Io(e) => e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe,
            _ => false,
        }
    }
}

    let mut state = OutputState {
        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
        at_line_start: true,
        skipped_carriage_return: false,
        one_blank_kept: false,
    };
    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();

    for path in files {
        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
        }
    }
    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
        print!("\r");
    }
    if error_messages.is_empty() {
        Ok(())
    } else {
        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());

        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(

            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),

    }
}' --new_str 'fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
    let mut state = OutputState {
        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
        at_line_start: true,
        skipped_carriage_return: false,
        one_blank_kept: false,
    };
    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();

    for path in files {
        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
            // BrokenPipe errors are normal when writing to a closed pipe
            // (e.g., piping to `head`), so we silently exit in that case.
            if err.is_broken_pipe() {
                return Ok(());
            }
            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
        }
    }
    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
        print!("\r");
    }
    if error_messages.is_empty() {
        Ok(())
    } else {
        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());

        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(
            error_messages.len() as i32,
            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),
        ))
    }
}'

Aha! The error is `Nix(EPIPE)`, not `Io(BrokenPipe)`! This is the key insight. On Linux/Android, the cat utility uses the splice() system call for faster writing, and when that fails with EPIPE, it's wrapped in `CatError::Nix` instead of `CatError::Io`.

Let me update the `is_broken_pipe` function to handle Nix errors as well:

    /// Check if this error is a BrokenPipe error, which should be ignored
    fn is_broken_pipe(&self) -> bool {

            CatError::Io(e) => e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe,
            _ => false,
        }
    }
}' --new_str 'impl CatError {
    /// Check if this error is a BrokenPipe error, which should be ignored
    fn is_broken_pipe(&self) -> bool {
        match self {
            CatError::Io(e) => e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe,
            #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
            CatError::Nix(e) => *e == nix::errno::Errno::EPIPE,
            _ => false,
        }
    }
}'

    exit 1

fi

echo "test content" > /tmp/test_cat.txt
output=$($CAT /tmp/test_cat.txt)
if [ "$output" = "test content" ]; then
    echo "✓ Test 3 passed: Normal file works"
else
    echo "✗ Test 3 failed: Output was: $output"
    exit 1
fi

echo "Test 4: cat multiple files with broken pipe (should not show error)"
output=$($CAT /tmp/test_cat.txt /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
if [ -z "$output" ]; then
    echo "✓ Test 4 passed: No error output with multiple files"
else
    echo "✗ Test 4 failed: Got error: $output"
    exit 1
fi

echo "Test 5: Verify exit code is 0 for broken pipe"
$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null
exit_code=$?
if [ $exit_code -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "✓ Test 5 passed: Exit code is 0"
else
    echo "✗ Test 5 failed: Exit code is $exit_code"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "All tests passed!"

   418	}
   419	
   420	fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
   421	    let mut state = OutputState {
   422	        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
   423	        at_line_start: true,
   424	        skipped_carriage_return: false,
   425	        one_blank_kept: false,
   426	    };
   427	    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();
   428	
   429	    for path in files {
   430	        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
   431	            // BrokenPipe errors are normal when writing to a closed pipe
   432	            // (e.g., piping to `head`), so we silently exit in that case.
   433	            if err.is_broken_pipe() {
   434	                return Ok(());
   435	            }
   436	            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
   437	        }
   438	    }
   439	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   440	        print!("\r");
   441	    }
   442	    if error_messages.is_empty() {
   443	        Ok(())
   444	    } else {
   445	        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
   446	        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());
   447	
   448	        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(
   449	            error_messages.len() as i32,
   450	            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),
   451	        ))
   452	    }

     1	// This file is part of the uutils coreutils package.
     2	//
     3	// For the full copyright and license information, please view the LICENSE
     4	// file that was distributed with this source code.
     5	use super::{CatResult, FdReadable, InputHandle};
     6	
     7	use nix::unistd;
     8	use std::os::{fd::AsFd, unix::io::AsRawFd};
     9	
    10	use uucore::pipes::{pipe, splice, splice_exact};
    11	
    12	const SPLICE_SIZE: usize = 1024 * 128;
    13	const BUF_SIZE: usize = 1024 * 16;
    14	
    15	/// This function is called from `write_fast()` on Linux and Android. The
    16	/// function `splice()` is used to move data between two file descriptors
    17	/// without copying between kernel and user spaces. This results in a large
    18	/// speedup.
    19	///
    20	/// The `bool` in the result value indicates if we need to fall back to normal
    21	/// copying or not. False means we don't have to.
    22	#[inline]
    23	pub(super) fn write_fast_using_splice<R: FdReadable, S: AsRawFd + AsFd>(
    24	    handle: &InputHandle<R>,
    25	    write_fd: &S,
    26	) -> CatResult<bool> {
    27	    let (pipe_rd, pipe_wr) = pipe()?;
    28	
    29	    loop {
    30	        match splice(&handle.reader, &pipe_wr, SPLICE_SIZE) {
    31	            Ok(n) => {
    32	                if n == 0 {
    33	                    return Ok(false);
    34	                }
    35	                if splice_exact(&pipe_rd, write_fd, n).is_err() {
    36	                    // If the first splice manages to copy to the intermediate
    37	                    // pipe, but the second splice to stdout fails for some reason
    38	                    // we can recover by copying the data that we have from the
    39	                    // intermediate pipe to stdout using normal read/write. Then
    40	                    // we tell the caller to fall back.
    41	                    copy_exact(&pipe_rd, write_fd, n)?;
    42	                    return Ok(true);
    43	                }
    44	            }
    45	            Err(_) => {
    46	                return Ok(true);
    47	            }
    48	        }
    49	    }
    50	}
    51	
    52	/// Move exactly `num_bytes` bytes from `read_fd` to `write_fd`.
    53	///
    54	/// Panics if not enough bytes can be read.
    55	fn copy_exact(read_fd: &impl AsFd, write_fd: &impl AsFd, num_bytes: usize) -> nix::Result<()> {
    56	    let mut left = num_bytes;
    57	    let mut buf = [0; BUF_SIZE];
    58	    while left > 0 {
    59	        let read = unistd::read(read_fd, &mut buf)?;
    60	        assert_ne!(read, 0, "unexpected end of pipe");
    61	        let mut written = 0;
    62	        while written < read {
    63	            match unistd::write(write_fd, &buf[written..read])? {
    64	                0 => panic!(),
    65	                n => written += n,
    66	            }
    67	        }
    68	        left -= read;
    69	    }
    70	    Ok(())
    71	}
    72

Now let's create a comprehensive test to ensure everything works:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/comprehensive_test.sh --file_text '#!/bin/bash

# Comprehensive test for broken pipe handling in cat

set -e

CAT="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils cat"
PASS_COUNT=0
FAIL_COUNT=0

test_case() {
    local name="$1"
    local command="$2"
    local expect_no_error="${3:-true}"
    
    echo -n "Testing: $name ... "
    
    stderr_output=$(eval "$command" 2>&1)
    
    if [ "$expect_no_error" = "true" ]; then
        if [ -z "$stderr_output" ]; then
            echo "✓ PASS"
            ((PASS_COUNT++))
        else
            echo "✗ FAIL (unexpected stderr: $stderr_output)"
            ((FAIL_COUNT++))
        fi
    else
        if [ -n "$stderr_output" ]; then
            echo "✓ PASS"
            ((PASS_COUNT++))
        else
            echo "✗ FAIL (expected error but got none)"
            ((FAIL_COUNT++))
        fi
    fi
}

echo "Running comprehensive broken pipe tests..."
echo ""

# Test 1: Basic broken pipe with /dev/zero
test_case "cat /dev/zero | head" "$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true

# Test 2: Broken pipe with stdin
test_case "yes | cat | head" "yes 2>/dev/null | $CAT 2>&1 | head -n 5 > /dev/null" true

# Test 3: Broken pipe with -n option (uses write_lines instead of write_fast)
test_case "cat -n /dev/zero | head" "$CAT -n /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true

# Test 4: Broken pipe with -A option
test_case "cat -A /dev/zero | head" "$CAT -A /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true

# Test 5: Multiple files with broken pipe
echo "test" > /tmp/cat_test.txt
test_case "cat multiple files | head" "$CAT /tmp/cat_test.txt /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true

# Test 6: Ensure real errors still show up
test_case "cat non-existent file" "$CAT /nonexistent 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null || true" false

# Test 7: Normal operation without pipe
echo "normal test" > /tmp/cat_test2.txt
output=$($CAT /tmp/cat_test2.txt 2>&1)
if [ "$output" = "normal test" ]; then
    echo "Testing: Normal file operation ... ✓ PASS"
    ((PASS_COUNT++))
else
    echo "Testing: Normal file operation ... ✗ FAIL"
    ((FAIL_COUNT++))
fi

# Test 8: Check exit code for broken pipe
$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null
exit_code=$?
if [ $exit_code -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "Testing: Exit code is 0 for broken pipe ... ✓ PASS"
    ((PASS_COUNT++))
else
    echo "Testing: Exit code is 0 for broken pipe ... ✗ FAIL (got $exit_code)"
    ((FAIL_COUNT++))
fi

echo ""
echo "=========================================="
echo "Test Results: $PASS_COUNT passed, $FAIL_COUNT failed"
echo "=========================================="

if [ $FAIL_COUNT -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "All tests passed! ✓"
    exit 0
else
    echo "Some tests failed! ✗"
    exit 1
fi
'

# Simple test for the broken pipe fix

output=$($CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
if [ -z "$output" ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: No error output"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got output: $output"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 2: cat with -n option and broken pipe"
output=$($CAT -n /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
if [ -z "$output" ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: No error output with -n option"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got output: $output"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 3: cat non-existent file (should show error)"
output=$($CAT /nonexistent 2>&1 || true)
if echo "$output" | grep -q "No such file"; then
    echo "✓ PASS: Error correctly shown for missing file"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Expected error not shown"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 4: Exit code should be 0 for broken pipe"
$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null
if [ $? -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: Exit code is 0"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Exit code is $?"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "===================="
echo "All tests passed! ✓"
echo "===================="
'

+    /// Check if this error is a BrokenPipe error, which should be ignored
+    fn is_broken_pipe(&self) -> bool {
+        match self {
+            CatError::Io(e) => e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe,
+            #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
+            CatError::Nix(e) => *e == nix::errno::Errno::EPIPE,
+            _ => false,
+        }
+    }
+}
+
 #[derive(PartialEq)]
 enum NumberingMode {
     None,
@@ -416,6 +428,11 @@ fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
 
     for path in files {
         if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
+            // BrokenPipe errors are normal when writing to a closed pipe
+            // (e.g., piping to `head`), so we silently exit in that case.
+            if err.is_broken_pipe() {
+                return Ok(());
+            }
             error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
         }
     }

## Summary of Changes

We made minimal changes to `/testbed/src/uu/cat/src/cat.rs`:

1. **Added `is_broken_pipe()` method to `CatError`** (lines 112-122):
   - Checks if a `CatError` is a BrokenPipe error
   - Handles both `io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe` (for regular I/O operations)
   - Handles `nix::errno::Errno::EPIPE` (for splice operations on Linux/Android)

2. **Modified `cat_files()` function** (lines 431-437):
   - Added a check for BrokenPipe errors before adding them to error messages
   - Returns `Ok(())` when a BrokenPipe error is detected, allowing the program to exit silently with exit code 0

These changes align with how other utilities in the codebase (like `seq` and `yes`) handle broken pipe errors.

# Edge case tests for the broken pipe fix

set -e

CAT="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils cat"

echo "Edge Case Tests"
echo "==============="
echo ""

# Test 1: Multiple files where first one causes error and second causes broken pipe

if echo "$output" | grep -q "No such file"; then
    echo "✓ PASS: First file error is reported"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Expected error from first file"
    exit 1
fi

# Test 2: Empty file followed by broken pipe
echo "" > /tmp/empty.txt
echo ""
echo "Test 2: Empty file followed by /dev/zero with broken pipe"
output=$($CAT /tmp/empty.txt /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
if [ -z "$output" ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: No error for empty file + broken pipe"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
    exit 1
fi

# Test 3: Regular file piped to head (no broken pipe because file ends before pipe closes)
echo "test content" > /tmp/short.txt
echo ""
echo "Test 3: Short file piped to head (pipe doesn'"'"'t break)"
output=$($CAT /tmp/short.txt 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
if [ -z "$output" ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: No error for short file"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
    exit 1
fi

# Test 4: Broken pipe with --show-all option
echo ""

if [ -z "$output" ]; then
    echo "✓ PASS: No error with --show-all"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
    exit 1
fi

# Test 5: Broken pipe with --squeeze-blank option

    echo "✓ PASS: No error with --squeeze-blank"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"

    echo "✓ PASS: No error with stdin + broken pipe"
else
    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"

   423	        at_line_start: true,
   424	        skipped_carriage_return: false,

   431	            // BrokenPipe errors are normal when writing to a closed pipe

+#!/bin/bash
+
+# Comprehensive test for broken pipe handling in cat
+
+set -e
+
+CAT="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils cat"
+PASS_COUNT=0
+FAIL_COUNT=0
+
+test_case() {
+    local name="$1"
+    local command="$2"
+    local expect_no_error="${3:-true}"
+    
+    echo -n "Testing: $name ... "
+    
+    stderr_output=$(eval "$command" 2>&1)
+    
+    if [ "$expect_no_error" = "true" ]; then
+        if [ -z "$stderr_output" ]; then
+            echo "✓ PASS"
+            ((PASS_COUNT++))
+        else
+            echo "✗ FAIL (unexpected stderr: $stderr_output)"
+            ((FAIL_COUNT++))
+        fi
+    else
+        if [ -n "$stderr_output" ]; then
+            echo "✓ PASS"
+            ((PASS_COUNT++))
+        else
+            echo "✗ FAIL (expected error but got none)"
+            ((FAIL_COUNT++))
+        fi
+    fi
+}
+
+echo "Running comprehensive broken pipe tests..."
+echo ""
+
+# Test 1: Basic broken pipe with /dev/zero
+test_case "cat /dev/zero | head" "$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true
+
+# Test 2: Broken pipe with stdin
+test_case "yes | cat | head" "yes 2>/dev/null | $CAT 2>&1 | head -n 5 > /dev/null" true
+
+# Test 3: Broken pipe with -n option (uses write_lines instead of write_fast)
+test_case "cat -n /dev/zero | head" "$CAT -n /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true
+
+# Test 4: Broken pipe with -A option
+test_case "cat -A /dev/zero | head" "$CAT -A /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true
+
+# Test 5: Multiple files with broken pipe
+echo "test" > /tmp/cat_test.txt
+test_case "cat multiple files | head" "$CAT /tmp/cat_test.txt /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null" true
+
+# Test 6: Ensure real errors still show up
+test_case "cat non-existent file" "$CAT /nonexistent 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null || true" false
+
+# Test 7: Normal operation without pipe
+echo "normal test" > /tmp/cat_test2.txt
+output=$($CAT /tmp/cat_test2.txt 2>&1)
+if [ "$output" = "normal test" ]; then
+    echo "Testing: Normal file operation ... ✓ PASS"
+    ((PASS_COUNT++))
+else
+    echo "Testing: Normal file operation ... ✗ FAIL"
+    ((FAIL_COUNT++))
+fi
+
+# Test 8: Check exit code for broken pipe
+$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null
+exit_code=$?
+if [ $exit_code -eq 0 ]; then
+    echo "Testing: Exit code is 0 for broken pipe ... ✓ PASS"
+    ((PASS_COUNT++))
+else
+    echo "Testing: Exit code is 0 for broken pipe ... ✗ FAIL (got $exit_code)"
+    ((FAIL_COUNT++))
+fi
+
+echo ""
+echo "=========================================="
+echo "Test Results: $PASS_COUNT passed, $FAIL_COUNT failed"
+echo "=========================================="
+
+if [ $FAIL_COUNT -eq 0 ]; then
+    echo "All tests passed! ✓"
+    exit 0
+else
+    echo "Some tests failed! ✗"

+#!/bin/bash
+
+# Edge case tests for the broken pipe fix
+
+set -e
+
+CAT="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils cat"
+
+echo "Edge Case Tests"
+echo "==============="
+echo ""
+
+# Test 1: Multiple files where first one causes error and second causes broken pipe
+echo "Test 1: Error on first file, then broken pipe on second"
+output=$($CAT /nonexistent /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null || true)
+if echo "$output" | grep -q "No such file"; then
+    echo "✓ PASS: First file error is reported"
+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Expected error from first file"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+# Test 2: Empty file followed by broken pipe
+echo "" > /tmp/empty.txt
+echo ""
+echo "Test 2: Empty file followed by /dev/zero with broken pipe"
+output=$($CAT /tmp/empty.txt /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ PASS: No error for empty file + broken pipe"
+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+# Test 3: Regular file piped to head (no broken pipe because file ends before pipe closes)
+echo "test content" > /tmp/short.txt
+echo ""
+echo "Test 3: Short file piped to head (pipe doesn't break)"
+output=$($CAT /tmp/short.txt 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ PASS: No error for short file"
+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+# Test 4: Broken pipe with --show-all option
+echo ""
+echo "Test 4: Broken pipe with --show-all option"
+output=$($CAT --show-all /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ PASS: No error with --show-all"
+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+# Test 5: Broken pipe with --squeeze-blank option
+echo ""
+echo "Test 5: Broken pipe with --squeeze-blank option"
+output=$($CAT --squeeze-blank /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ PASS: No error with --squeeze-blank"
+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+# Test 6: stdin with broken pipe
+echo ""
+echo "Test 6: Reading from stdin with broken pipe"
+output=$(echo "test" | $CAT - /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ PASS: No error with stdin + broken pipe"
+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Got unexpected output: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo ""
+echo "========================"
+echo "All edge case tests passed! ✓"
+echo "========================"

+#!/bin/bash

+else
+    echo "✗ FAIL: Got output: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi

+output=$($CAT -n /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then

+    exit 1

@@ -109,6 +109,18 @@ enum CatError {
 
 type CatResult<T> = Result<T, CatError>;
 
+impl CatError {
+    /// Check if this error is a BrokenPipe error, which should be ignored
+    fn is_broken_pipe(&self) -> bool {
+        match self {
+            CatError::Io(e) => e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe,
+            #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
+            CatError::Nix(e) => *e == nix::errno::Errno::EPIPE,
+            _ => false,
+        }
+    }
+}
+
 #[derive(PartialEq)]
 enum NumberingMode {
     None,
@@ -416,6 +428,12 @@ fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
 
     for path in files {
         if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
+            // BrokenPipe errors are normal when writing to a closed pipe
+            // (e.g., piping to `head`), so we silently stop processing files.
+            // However, we still report any errors that occurred before the broken pipe.
+            if err.is_broken_pipe() {
+                break;
+            }
             error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
         }
     }

+#!/bin/bash
+
+# Test the broken pipe behavior
+# This mimics what the fish shell test is doing
+
+# Build the cat utility first
+cd /testbed
+cargo build --release --bin cat 2>&1 | tail -5
+
+# Create a test with /dev/zero and head (which closes the pipe early)
+echo "Testing broken pipe with /dev/zero..."
+timeout 2 /testbed/target/release/cat /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 1000 > /dev/null
+
+# Check the exit status
+if [ $? -eq 0 ] || [ $? -eq 141 ]; then
+    echo "✓ Test passed: No EPIPE error shown"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test failed with exit code: $?"
+fi
+
+# Also test with a simple echo | head scenario
+echo "Testing broken pipe with echo..."
+yes | /testbed/target/release/cat 2>&1 | head -n 5 > /dev/null
+
+if [ $? -eq 0 ] || [ $? -eq 141 ]; then
+    echo "✓ Test passed: No EPIPE error shown"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test failed with exit code: $?"
+fi

+#!/bin/bash
+
+set -e
+
+CAT="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils cat"
+
+echo "Test 1: cat /dev/zero piped to head (should not show error)"
+output=$($CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ Test 1 passed: No error output"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test 1 failed: Got error: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "Test 2: cat with non-existent file (should show error)"
+output=$($CAT /nonexistent 2>&1 || true)
+if echo "$output" | grep -q "No such file"; then
+    echo "✓ Test 2 passed: Error shown for missing file"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test 2 failed: Expected error not shown"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "Test 3: cat normal file (should work)"
+echo "test content" > /tmp/test_cat.txt
+output=$($CAT /tmp/test_cat.txt)
+if [ "$output" = "test content" ]; then
+    echo "✓ Test 3 passed: Normal file works"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test 3 failed: Output was: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "Test 4: cat multiple files with broken pipe (should not show error)"
+output=$($CAT /tmp/test_cat.txt /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null)
+if [ -z "$output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ Test 4 passed: No error output with multiple files"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test 4 failed: Got error: $output"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo "Test 5: Verify exit code is 0 for broken pipe"
+$CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 100 > /dev/null
+exit_code=$?
+if [ $exit_code -eq 0 ]; then
+    echo "✓ Test 5 passed: Exit code is 0"
+else
+    echo "✗ Test 5 failed: Exit code is $exit_code"
+    exit 1
+fi
+
+echo ""
+echo "All tests passed!"

+#!/bin/bash
+
+# This script simulates the scenario from the fish shell test
+# that was originally failing
+
+set -e
+
+CAT="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils cat"
+
+echo "Simulating fish shell pipestatus test scenario..."
+echo ""
+
+# The fish test was checking that no broken pipe error appears on stderr
+# when cat reads from /dev/zero and the downstream process closes the pipe
+
+echo "Running: cat /dev/zero | head -c 1000"
+stderr_output=$($CAT /dev/zero 2>&1 | head -c 1000 > /dev/null 2>&1)
+
+if [ -z "$stderr_output" ]; then
+    echo "✓ SUCCESS: No broken pipe error was shown (stderr is empty)"
+    exit 0
+else
+    echo "✗ FAILURE: Unexpected output on stderr:"
+    echo "$stderr_output"
+    exit 1
+fi
